Choices:

  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:

  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of odontogenic cyst that forms around the crown of an unerupted tooth. It can cause swelling, pain, and displacement of teeth, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a fracture of one or more of the bones that form the orbit. It can cause swelling, bruising, and double vision, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition in which the temporomandibular joint (TMJ) becomes fused, making it difficult or impossible to open the mouth. This can cause difficulty eating and speaking, but it is also known to cause obstructive sleep apnea due to the inability to properly position the tongue and airway during sleep.

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  High levels of LDL and TG and low levels of HDL are risk factors for cardiovascular diseases.
  Statins and fibrates are commonly used medications to manage cholesterol levels.
  Rosuvastatin and atorvastatin are statins.
  Fenofibrate is a fibrate.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that requires immediate treatment. It occurs when the blood flow that brings oxygen to the heart muscle is severely reduced or cut off completely.
  Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the amount of cholesterol and fats called triglycerides in the blood.
  HDL (High-density lipoprotein) is known as the "good" cholesterol because it helps remove LDL (Low-density lipoprotein) or "bad" cholesterol from the arteries.
  LDL (Low-density lipoprotein) is known as the "bad" cholesterol because it can build up in the walls of arteries and form plaques, which can lead to heart disease and stroke.
  TG (Triglycerides) are a type of fat (lipid) found in the blood. High levels of triglycerides can increase the risk of heart disease.
  Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are medications used to lower cholesterol levels in the blood.
  Fenofibrate is a medication used to lower triglyceride levels in the blood.
  
Analysis:
  The patient had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back and has abnormal lipid profile with low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels. The preferred medication for this patient should be one that can lower LDL and TG levels while increasing HDL levels. Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin can lower LDL levels, but they do not increase HDL levels. Fenofibrate can lower TG levels and increase HDL levels, but it does not lower LDL levels. Therefore, the preferred medication for this patient should be a combination of a statin (to lower LDL levels) and fenofibrate (to lower TG levels and increase HDL levels).
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction is a medical emergency that requires immediate treatment.
  HDL, LDL, and TG are types of cholesterol that are measured in a lipid profile.
  High levels of LDL and TG, and low levels of HDL are risk factors for cardiovascular disease.
  Statins are drugs that can lower LDL cholesterol levels, while fibrates can lower TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  Combination therapy with a statin and a fibrate may be considered in patients with high TG and low HDL levels.
  
Analysis:
  The patient has high TG and low HDL levels, which suggests that a fibrate may be beneficial.
  The patient also has high LDL levels, which suggests that a statin may be beneficial.
  Combination therapy with a statin and a fibrate may be considered in patients with high TG and low HDL levels.

Action: Answer("A")

  Fibrates are another class of drugs that lower triglyceride levels and increase HDL cholesterol levels.

Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body

  The third ventricle is a cavity in the brain that is continuous with the lateral ventricles via the interventricular foramen (foramen of Monro).
  A: The optic stalk is a structure that connects the optic nerve to the hypothalamus and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve (oculomotor nerve) is a cranial nerve that controls the movement of the eye and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain that are involved in memory and are not present on the floor of the third ventricle.

  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  T4 and TSH are hormones produced by the thyroid gland.
  Low T4 and raised TSH indicate hypothyroidism.
  Pituitary gland is responsible for producing TSH.
  Swelling or tumor of the pituitary gland may cause an excess production of TSH.
  
Action: Answer("C")  
The symptoms suggest a TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma, which is a type of pituitary tumor that secretes excess TSH leading to hyperstimulation of the thyroid gland. This results in increased thyroid hormone production which suppresses TSH secretion from the pituitary gland. However, in some cases, the tumor may be large enough to cause compression of surrounding structures leading to symptoms such as headache or visual disturbances.

Question: Which of the following show chemical bond with enamel (calcified tissues)?
Choices:
  A: Composites
  B: Direct filling resins
  C: Polycarboxylate cements
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Composites are a type of dental filling material that bond to teeth mechanically, not chemically.
  B: Direct filling resins are a type of dental filling material that bond to teeth through a chemical bond with enamel.
  C: Polycarboxylate cements are a type of dental cement that bond to teeth through a chemical bond with enamel.
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants are a type of dental material that bond to teeth through a chemical bond with enamel.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Composites are tooth-colored restorative materials made from a mixture of glass or ceramic filler particles and a resin matrix. They bond to enamel and dentin through a process called micromechanical retention, where the resin flows into the porosities of the etched enamel and forms tags or resin tags that anchor the composite to the tooth.
  B: Direct filling resins are a type of composite that is used for restoring cavities and other defects in teeth. They also bond to enamel and dentin through micromechanical retention.
  C: Polycarboxylate cements are a type of dental cement used for luting crowns, bridges, and other restorations. They bond to enamel and dentin through chemical bonding, where the carboxylic acid groups in the cement react with the calcium ions in the tooth structure.
  D: BIS-GMA resins are a type of resin used in pit and fissure sealants, which are thin plastic coatings applied to the chewing surfaces of molars and premolars to prevent cavities. They bond to enamel through micromechanical retention.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  A: Composites are tooth-colored fillings made of a mixture of glass or quartz filler and a resin bonding material. They bond to the tooth structure through a chemical reaction.
  B: Direct filling resins are also known as dental bonding. They are made of a resin material that is chemically bonded to the tooth.
  C: Polycarboxylate cements are dental cements that bond chemically to enamel and dentin.
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants bond to enamel through a chemical reaction.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  A: Composites are tooth-colored restorative materials that are composed of a resin matrix and inorganic filler particles. They bond to enamel by micromechanical interlocking.
  B: Direct filling resins are also composite materials that bond to enamel by micromechanical interlocking.
  C: Polycarboxylate cements are dental cements that bond to enamel by chemical bonding (ionic bond) between the carboxylate groups in the cement and the calcium ions in the enamel.
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants are also composite materials that bond to enamel by micromechanical interlocking.

Knowledge:

  B: B>D>C>A
  C: A>D>B>C

  The auditory pathway starts from the cochlea and ends in the auditory cortex.
  The cochlear nucleus is the first structure in the auditory pathway, which receives input from the cochlea.
  The inferior colliculus is the next structure in the auditory pathway, which receives input from the superior olivary complex.
  The medial geniculate body is the last structure in the subcortical auditory pathway, which receives input from the inferior colliculus and projects to the auditory cortex.

Action: Answer("A")  
The correct sequence of the auditory pathway from peripheral to central is Cochlear nucleus > Auditory coex > Inferior colliculus > Medial geniculate body. Therefore, the correct answer is A: B>A>D>C.

Question: A patient sustained A and endotracheal intubation was done. Most likely GCS score of such a patient would be:March 2013 (b, c, d)
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 10
  C: 12
  D: 15
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  GCS (Glasgow Coma Scale) is a neurological scale that aims to give a reliable and objective way of recording the conscious state of a person for initial as well as subsequent assessment.
  The scale has three components: eye response, verbal response, and motor response.
  The maximum score is 15 and the minimum score is 3.
  A: A GCS score of 8 indicates a severe brain injury.
  B: A GCS score of 10 indicates a moderate brain injury.
  C: A GCS score of 12 indicates a mild brain injury.
  D: A GCS score of 15 indicates a fully awake and alert person.
  
Action: Answer("B")  
Explanation: Endotracheal intubation is a procedure used to establish an airway in patients who are unable to breathe on their own. This procedure is usually done in patients who have sustained a severe injury or illness. A patient who has undergone endotracheal intubation is likely to have a moderate brain injury, which would correspond to a GCS score of 10.

The lowest possible GCS (the sum) is 3 (deep coma or death), while the highest is 15 (fully awake person).

Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a periodontal surgery technique used to access and treat the root surface of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years have been exposed to the oral environment for a long time, which can lead to changes in the periodontal structures.
  A: The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the cementum to the alveolar bone, but in a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibres may have been lost or damaged.
  B: The PDL fibres attach the cementum to the alveolar bone, but in a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years, the cementum may have been lost or damaged, leaving the dentin exposed.
  C: The epithelium adjacent to a previously denuded root surface may have become hyperkeratinized and may not allow for proper healing and attachment of the PDL fibres.
  D: Co-adaptation to the remaining fibres may occur, but the remaining fibres may not be sufficient to support the tooth properly.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure where the gum tissue is cut and moved laterally to expose the underlying tooth root.
  - The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a group of fibers that attach the tooth root to the surrounding bone.
  - Root denudation is a condition where the tooth root becomes exposed due to loss of gum tissue.
  
A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum - This is not likely to be seen, as the roots have been denuded for 6 years, which would have caused the cementum to wear away.
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin - This is not likely to be seen, as the roots have been denuded for 6 years, which would have caused the dentin to be exposed and possibly damaged.
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface - This is likely to be seen, as the body will have attempted to repair the denuded area by growing new epithelial cells around the exposed root surface.
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres - This choice is not clear, as it is not specific enough to the situation described in the question.

Action: Answer("C")

Option B: PDL fibres are not normally attached to dentin, which is the softer, more porous tissue that forms the bulk of the tooth structure.
Option C: Epithelial attachment occurs when the epithelial cells attach to the root surface instead of the gingival tissue. This can occur as a result of chronic inflammation or trauma.
Option D: Co-adaptation refers to the process by which the PDL fibres reattach to the root surface after a period of denudation.

  C: Long half-life permits altemate day dosing

  B: Hysteroscopy is a procedure that involves the insertion of a thin, lighted tube through the vagina and cervix into the uterus to examine the inside of the uterus.
  C: Endometrial biopsy is a procedure that involves the removal of a small piece of tissue from the lining of the uterus (endometrium) for examination.
  D: Chromosomal abnormalities can cause pregnancy loss and may be investigated if there is a history of recurrent pregnancy loss.
  
Based on the given history, the most likely cause of second trimester abortions is cervical incompetence or uterine anomalies. Therefore, the next investigation that is usually advised is TVS to evaluate the uterus and cervix.

  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - Dummer's classification is used to categorize the root canal morphology of teeth.
  - Multi constricted apical constriction refers to the presence of multiple constrictions near the apex of the root canal.
  - Type 1: A single canal from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  - Type 2: Two separate canals leaving the pulp chamber but merging into one canal short of the apex.
  - Type 3: Two separate and distinct canals extend from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  - Type 4: Multiple canals, including separate and distinct accessory canals, are present in the apical third of the root canal system.

  D: Flexibility is the ability to adapt to changing circumstances.

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Proteinuria is the presence of excess proteins in the urine and is a sign of kidney damage or dysfunction.
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Severe preeclampsia is a more severe form of preeclampsia.
  The diagnostic criteria for severe preeclampsia include a systolic blood pressure of 160 mm Hg or higher and/or a diastolic blood pressure of 110 mm Hg or higher, along with other symptoms such as proteinuria.
Action: Answer("C") 
The level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is typically 300 mg or more in a 24-hour urine collection or a urine protein-to-creatinine ratio of 0.3 or higher.

Topic: Pediatrics
Question: A neonate presents with jaundice and clay coloured stools. Liver biopsy shows giant cells diagnosis is –
Choices:
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Jaundice is a yellow discoloration of the skin and mucous membranes due to increased levels of bilirubin in the blood.
  - Clay-colored stools can be a sign of a problem with the bile ducts.
  - Giant cells are a type of inflammatory cells that can be seen in liver biopsy specimens in different conditions, including viral hepatitis and biliary atresia.
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice is a condition where the newborn baby's liver is inflamed and unable to function properly, leading to jaundice. However, clay-colored stools are not typically seen in this condition.
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia is a condition where the bile ducts outside the liver are blocked or absent, leading to jaundice and clay-colored stools. Giant cells can be seen in liver biopsy specimens in this condition.
  C: Physiological jaundice is a common condition in newborns where the liver is still developing and unable to process bilirubin efficiently, leading to mild jaundice. However, clay-colored stools are not typically seen in this condition.
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia is not a recognized medical condition.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Neonate refers to a newborn baby.
  Jaundice is a yellowish discoloration of the skin and mucous membranes due to the accumulation of bilirubin in the blood.
  Clay-colored stools can be a sign of liver disease.
  Liver biopsy is a procedure used to obtain a small piece of liver tissue for examination under a microscope.
  Giant cells can be seen in viral hepatitis, autoimmune hepatitis, and drug-induced hepatitis.
A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice is a possibility, but the presence of clay-colored stools and giant cells suggests a more severe condition.
B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia is a possibility, as this condition can cause jaundice and clay-colored stools. Giant cells can also be seen in this condition.
C: Physiological jaundice is a common condition in newborns, but it does not typically cause clay-colored stools or giant cells on liver biopsy.
D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia is not a recognized diagnosis.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  1. Jaundice is a common condition in neonates and can be caused by various conditions.
  2. Clay-colored stools are indicative of biliary obstruction.
  3. Giant cells are typically seen in viral hepatitis.

  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling

Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling involves selecting every nth individual from a list or population.
  B: Simple random sampling involves selecting individuals randomly from a list or population.
  C: Stratified random sampling involves dividing a population into subgroups or strata and then selecting individuals randomly from each subgroup.
  D: Cluster sampling involves dividing a population into clusters or groups, randomly selecting some of the clusters, and then selecting all individuals within the selected clusters.

Answer: C
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling involves selecting every nth individual from a list or sampling frame.
  B: Simple random sampling involves selecting individuals randomly from a list or sampling frame.
  C: Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into strata and randomly selecting individuals from each stratum.
  D: Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into clusters and randomly selecting entire clusters to sample.
  
Since the question is asking about selecting patients based on potential factors affecting the results, the most appropriate sampling method would be stratified random sampling where the population is divided into strata based on the potential factors and individuals are randomly selected from each stratum.

  D: Cluster sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a population in which the population is divided into clusters (or groups) and then a random sample of clusters is selected for inclusion in the study.
